from launch import LaunchDescription
from launch.actions import DeclareLaunchArgument, IncludeLaunchDescription, TimerAction
from launch.launch_description_sources import PythonLaunchDescriptionSource
from launch.substitutions import LaunchConfiguration, PathJoinSubstitution
from launch_ros.actions import Node
from launch_ros.substitutions import FindPackageShare

def generate_launch_description():
    # Arguments
    use_sim_time = LaunchConfiguration('use_sim_time', default='true')

    # Paths
    robot_gazebo_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_gazebo')
    moveit_config_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_moveit_config')
    robot_analysis_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_analysis')

    # 1. Gazebo Simulation (Physics + Controllers)
    # This launches Gazebo, Spawns Robot, and Starts ros2_control Controller Manager
    gazebo_launch = IncludeLaunchDescription(
        PythonLaunchDescriptionSource(
            PathJoinSubstitution([robot_gazebo_pkg, 'launch', 'gazebo.launch.py'])
        )
    )

    # 2. MoveIt (Motion Planning)
    # Configured to talk to Gazebo's /follow_joint_trajectory Action Server
    move_group_launch = IncludeLaunchDescription(
        PythonLaunchDescriptionSource(
            PathJoinSubstitution([moveit_config_pkg, 'launch', 'move_group.launch.py'])
        ),
        launch_arguments={
            'allow_trajectory_execution': 'true',
            'fake_execution': 'false',
            'info': 'true',
            'use_sim_time': use_sim_time
        }.items()
    )

    # 3. Accuracy Analysis (Observability)
    accuracy_node = Node(
        package='robot_analysis',
        executable='accuracy_node',
        name='accuracy_analysis',
        output='screen'
    )

    return LaunchDescription([
        gazebo_launch,
        # Delayed MoveIt to wait for Gazebo
        TimerAction(
            period=10.0,
            actions=[move_group_launch]
        ),
        accuracy_node
    ])

mode_real.launch.py
from launch import LaunchDescription
from launch.actions import DeclareLaunchArgument, IncludeLaunchDescription, TimerAction
from launch.launch_description_sources import PythonLaunchDescriptionSource
from launch.substitutions import LaunchConfiguration, PathJoinSubstitution
from launch_ros.actions import Node
from launch_ros.substitutions import FindPackageShare

def generate_launch_description():
    # Arguments
    use_sim_time = LaunchConfiguration('use_sim_time', default='false')

    # Paths
    robot_description_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_description')
    moveit_config_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_moveit_config')
    hardware_bridge_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_hardware_bridge')
    robot_analysis_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_analysis')

    # 1. State Publisher (URDF) - Source of Truth for TF
    display_launch = IncludeLaunchDescription(
        PythonLaunchDescriptionSource(
            PathJoinSubstitution([robot_description_pkg, 'launch', 'display.launch.py'])
        ),
        launch_arguments={'use_sim_time': use_sim_time}.items()
    )

    # 2. Hardware Bridge (The Adapter to ESP32)
    # This node is the Gateway. It subscribes to /planned_trajectory and publishes to ESP32.
    # It also receives /joint_states from ESP32.
    bridge_node = Node(
        package='robot_hardware_bridge',
        executable='bridge_node',
        name='hardware_bridge',
        output='screen',
        parameters=[{'controller_ip': '192.168.1.100', 'mode': 'REAL'}]
    )

    # 3. MoveIt Adapter (The Action Server)
    # Converts MoveIt's FollowJointTrajectory Action -> /planned_trajectory Topic
    moveit_adapter = Node(
        package='robot_hardware_bridge',
        executable='moveit_adapter',
        name='moveit_adapter',
        output='screen'
    )

    # 4. MoveIt (Motion Planning)
    # Launches move_group without Sim Controllers
    # We must ensure it listens to /joint_states from the Bridge
    move_group_launch = IncludeLaunchDescription(
        PythonLaunchDescriptionSource(
            PathJoinSubstitution([moveit_config_pkg, 'launch', 'move_group.launch.py'])
        ),
        launch_arguments={
            'allow_trajectory_execution': 'true',
            'fake_execution': 'false',
            'info': 'true',
            'use_sim_time': use_sim_time
        }.items()
    )

    # 5. Accuracy Analysis (Observability)
    accuracy_node = Node(
        package='robot_analysis',
        executable='accuracy_node',
        name='accuracy_analysis',
        output='screen'
    )

    # 6. Rviz (Visualization)
    # MoveIt launch usually includes Rviz, but if not we can add it here.
    # For now, relying on move_group.launch.py to include Rviz if configured,
    # OR we can add a specific Rviz node if needed for "Mirror".
    # The 'display.launch.py' also usually launches Rviz.

    return LaunchDescription([
        display_launch,
        bridge_node,
        moveit_adapter,
        # Delayed launch for MoveIt to ensure URDF is ready
        TimerAction(
            period=5.0,
            actions=[move_group_launch]
        ),
        accuracy_node
    ])
▼ Show more
ReadFile

display.launch.py
import os
from ament_index_python.packages import get_package_share_directory
from launch import LaunchDescription
from launch.substitutions import Command, LaunchConfiguration
from launch.actions import DeclareLaunchArgument
from launch_ros.actions import Node

def generate_launch_description():
    pkg_share = get_package_share_directory('robot_description')
    default_urdf = os.path.join(pkg_share, 'urdf', 'custom_6axis_test.urdf.xacro')

    return LaunchDescription([
        DeclareLaunchArgument(
            'model',
            default_value=default_urdf,
            description='Absolute path to robot urdf file'
        ),
        Node(
            package='robot_state_publisher',
            executable='robot_state_publisher',
            name='robot_state_publisher',
            output='screen',
            parameters=[{'robot_description': Command(['xacro ', LaunchConfiguration('model')])}]
        )
    ])

# Joint Limits for ABB IRB 120

joint_limits:
  joint_1:
    has_velocity_limits: true
    max_velocity: 4.363  # 250 deg/s
    has_acceleration_limits: true
    max_acceleration: 10.0
    has_position_limits: true
    min_position: -2.879 # -165 deg
    max_position: 2.879  # +165 deg

  joint_2:
    has_velocity_limits: true
    max_velocity: 4.363
    has_acceleration_limits: true

<?xml version="1.0"?>
<!--
  ABB IRB 120 URDF Description (Clean Room Implementation)

  Model: ABB IRB 120
  Reach: 580 mm
  Payload: 3 kg

  AUTHORITY NOTE:
  This file governs KINEMATICS only.
  Safety limits are enforced by the RT Controller.
  Simulated limits are enforced by MoveIt and Sim Backend.
-->
<robot xmlns:xacro="http://www.ros.org/wiki/xacro" name="robot_arm">

  <!-- Robot Parameters (ABB IRB 120) -->
  <xacro:property name="PI" value="3.14159265359"/>
  <xacro:property name="DEG2RAD" value="0.01745329251"/>

  <!-- Link Masses (Approximate distribution for 25kg total mass) -->
  <xacro:property name="mass_base" value="6.0"/>
  <xacro:property name="mass_link1" value="5.0"/>
  <xacro:property name="mass_link2" value="6.0"/>
  <xacro:property name="mass_link3" value="3.0"/>
  <xacro:property name="mass_link4" value="2.0"/>
  <xacro:property name="mass_link5" value="1.0"/>
  <xacro:property name="mass_link6" value="0.5"/>

  <!-- Reference Material -->
  <material name="abb_white">
    <color rgba="0.9 0.9 0.9 1"/>
  </material>
  <material name="abb_orange">
    <color rgba="1.0 0.5 0.0 1"/>
  </material>

  <!-- Dummy root link to satisfy KDL parser & Gazebo -->
  <link name="world"/>

  <joint name="fixed_base_joint" type="fixed">
    <parent link="world"/>
    <child link="base_link"/>
    <origin xyz="0 0 0" rpy="0 0 0"/>
  </joint>

  <!-- ======================== LINKS & JOINTS ======================== -->

  <!-- ============== BASE LINK ============== -->
  <link name="base_link">
    <visual>
      <geometry>
        <mesh filename="package://robot_description/meshes/base_link.stl" scale="0.001 0.001 0.001"/>
        <!-- Fallback geometry if mesh missing -->
        <box size="0.2 0.2 0.2"/>
      </geometry>
      <origin xyz="0 0 0.1" rpy="0 0 0"/>
      <material name="abb_orange"/>
    </visual>
    <collision>
      <geometry>
        <box size="0.2 0.2 0.2"/>
      </geometry>
      <origin xyz="0 0 0.1" rpy="0 0 0"/>
    </collision>
    <inertial>
      <mass value="${mass_base}"/>
      <inertia ixx="0.02" ixy="0" ixz="0" iyy="0.02" iyz="0" izz="0.02"/>
    </inertial>
  </link>

  <!-- ============== JOINT 1 (Base Rotation) ============== -->
  <!-- Height: 290mm from base to J2. Split: Base->J1 (Vertical) -->
  <joint name="joint_1" type="revolute">
    <parent link="base_link"/>
    <child link="link_1"/>
    <origin xyz="0 0 0.0" rpy="0 0 0"/>
    <axis xyz="0 0 1"/>
    <limit lower="${-165*DEG2RAD}" upper="${165*DEG2RAD}" effort="100" velocity="${250*DEG2RAD}"/>
    <dynamics damping="0.5" friction="0.1"/>
  </joint>

  <link name="link_1">
    <visual>
      <geometry>
        <cylinder radius="0.07" length="0.29"/>
      </geometry>
      <origin xyz="0 0 0.145" rpy="0 0 0"/>
      <material name="abb_orange"/>
    </visual>
    <collision>
      <geometry>
        <cylinder radius="0.07" length="0.29"/>
      </geometry>
      <origin xyz="0 0 0.145" rpy="0 0 0"/>
    </collision>
    <inertial>
      <mass value="${mass_link1}"/>
      <inertia ixx="0.01" ixy="0" ixz="0" iyy="0.01" iyz="0" izz="0.005"/>
    </inertial>
  </link>

  <!-- ============== JOINT 2 (Shoulder Bending) ============== -->
  <!-- Z: 290mm up. Axis Y -->
  <joint name="joint_2" type="revolute">
    <parent link="link_1"/>
    <child link="link_2"/>
    <origin xyz="0 0 0.290" rpy="0 0 0"/>
    <axis xyz="0 1 0"/>
    <limit lower="${-110*DEG2RAD}" upper="${110*DEG2RAD}" effort="100" velocity="${250*DEG2RAD}"/>
    <dynamics damping="0.5" friction="0.1"/>
  </joint>

  <link name="link_2">
    <visual>
      <geometry>
        <box size="0.05 0.05 0.270"/>

  <link name="link_3">
    <!-- Represents horizontal arm part: 70mm offset?

    </inertial>

cmake_minimum_required(VERSION 3.8)
project(robot_description)

find_package(ament_cmake REQUIRED)

# Install URDF files
install(DIRECTORY urdf/
  DESTINATION share/${PROJECT_NAME}/urdf
)

# Install mesh files
install(DIRECTORY meshes/
  DESTINATION share/${PROJECT_NAME}/meshes
)

# Install config files
install(DIRECTORY config/
  DESTINATION share/${PROJECT_NAME}/config
)

# Install launch files
install(DIRECTORY launch/
  DESTINATION share/${PROJECT_NAME}/launch
)

ReadFile

gazebo.launch.py
"""
Gazebo Harmonic Launch File - FIXED

AUTHORITY: EMULATED (No Real Authority)

This launch file starts Gazebo Harmonic simulation which:
- Provides physics emulation (NON-RT, NON-CERTIFIED)
- Spawns the robot model
- Runs simulated controllers

WARNING: SIM mode does not constitute safety validation.
All safety testing must be with real hardware in controlled conditions.
"""
from launch import LaunchDescription
from launch.actions import (
    DeclareLaunchArgument,
    IncludeLaunchDescription,
    ExecuteProcess,
    RegisterEventHandler,
    TimerAction,
)
from launch.conditions import IfCondition, UnlessCondition
from launch.substitutions import LaunchConfiguration, PathJoinSubstitution, Command
from launch.launch_description_sources import PythonLaunchDescriptionSource
from launch_ros.actions import Node
from launch_ros.substitutions import FindPackageShare
from launch_ros.parameter_descriptions import ParameterValue

def generate_launch_description():
    # Declare arguments
    headless = LaunchConfiguration('headless', default='false')
    world = LaunchConfiguration('world', default='empty.sdf')
    use_sim_time = LaunchConfiguration('use_sim_time', default='true')

    # Package paths
    robot_description_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_description')
    robot_gazebo_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_gazebo')
    ros_gz_sim_pkg = FindPackageShare('ros_gz_sim')

    # Robot description
    robot_description_path = PathJoinSubstitution([
        robot_description_pkg, 'urdf', 'ur3e_cobot_gazebo.urdf.xacro'
    ])

    robot_description = Command(['xacro ', robot_description_path], on_stderr='warn')

    # World file
    world_path = world

    # Gazebo Harmonic (gz_sim) - Headless
    gazebo_sim = IncludeLaunchDescription(
        PythonLaunchDescriptionSource([
            PathJoinSubstitution([ros_gz_sim_pkg, 'launch', 'gz_sim.launch.py'])
        ]),
        launch_arguments={'gz_args': ['-r -s -v4 ', world_path]}.items(),
        condition=IfCondition(headless)
    )

    # Gazebo Harmonic (gz_sim) - GUI
    gazebo_sim_gui = IncludeLaunchDescription(
        PythonLaunchDescriptionSource([
            PathJoinSubstitution([ros_gz_sim_pkg, 'launch', 'gz_sim.launch.py'])
        ]),
        launch_arguments={'gz_args': ['-r -v4 ', world_path]}.items(),
        condition=UnlessCondition(headless)
    )

    # Robot state publisher
    robot_state_publisher = Node(
        package='robot_state_publisher',
        executable='robot_state_publisher',
        output='screen',
        parameters=[{
            'robot_description': ParameterValue(robot_description, value_type=str),
            'use_sim_time': use_sim_time,
        }]
    )

    # Generate SDF and spawn robot in Gazebo Harmonic
    generate_sdf = ExecuteProcess(
        cmd=['bash', '-c', ['xacro ', robot_description_path, ' > /tmp/robot.urdf && gz sdf -p /tmp/robot.urdf > /tmp/robot.sdf']],
        output='screen'
    )

    spawn_robot = Node(
        package='ros_gz_sim',
        executable='create',
        arguments=[
            '-name', 'robot_arm',
            '-file', '/tmp/robot.sdf',
            '-x', '0', '-y', '0', '-z', '0',
        ],
        output='screen',
    )

    # Bridge for ROS 2 <-> Gazebo Harmonic
    bridge = Node(
        package='ros_gz_bridge',
        executable='parameter_bridge',
        arguments=[
            '/clock@rosgraph_msgs/msg/Clock[gz.msgs.Clock',
            '/gazebo/joint_states@sensor_msgs/msg/JointState[gz.msgs.Model',
            '/gazebo/joint_trajectory@trajectory_msgs/msg/JointTrajectory]gz.msgs.JointTrajectory',
        ],
        remappings=[
            ('/gazebo/joint_states', '/joint_states'),
            ('/gazebo/joint_trajectory', '/robot_arm_controller/joint_trajectory'),
        ],
        output='screen'
    )

    # Joint state broadcaster
    joint_state_broadcaster_spawner = TimerAction(
        period=5.0,
        actions=[
            Node(
                package='controller_manager',
                executable='spawner',
                arguments=['joint_state_broadcaster', '-c', '/controller_manager', '--controller-manager-timeout', '60'],
                output='screen',
            )
        ]
    )

    # Robot arm controller
    robot_arm_controller_spawner = TimerAction(
        period=8.0,
        actions=[
            Node(
                package='controller_manager',
                executable='spawner',
                arguments=['robot_arm_controller', '-c', '/controller_manager', '--controller-manager-timeout', '60'],
                output='screen',
            )
        ]
    )

    return LaunchDescription([
        DeclareLaunchArgument('headless', default_value='false', description='Run Gazebo headless'),
        DeclareLaunchArgument('world', default_value='empty.sdf', description='World file to load'),
        DeclareLaunchArgument('use_sim_time', default_value='true', description='Use simulation time'),

        gazebo_sim,
        gazebo_sim_gui,
        bridge,
        robot_state_publisher,
        generate_sdf,
        TimerAction(period=2.0, actions=[spawn_robot]),
        joint_state_broadcaster_spawner,
        robot_arm_controller_spawner,
    ])
▼ Show more
ReadFile

gazebo_controllers.yaml
# Gazebo Controller Configuration
# These controllers run inside Gazebo (NON-RT)
# They emulate the real controller for SIM mode testing

controller_manager:
  ros__parameters:
    update_rate: 1000  # Hz (simulated, not guaranteed)

    joint_state_broadcaster:
      type: joint_state_broadcaster/JointStateBroadcaster

    robot_arm_controller:
      type: joint_trajectory_controller/JointTrajectoryController

robot_arm_controller:
  ros__parameters:
    joints:
      - joint_1
      - joint_2
      - joint_3
      - joint_4
      - joint_5
      - joint_6

    command_interfaces:
      - position

    state_interfaces:
      - position
      - velocity

    state_publish_rate: 100.0
    action_monitor_rate: 20.0

    allow_partial_joints_goal: false
    open_loop_control: false

    constraints:
      stopped_velocity_tolerance: 0.01
      goal_time: 0.0

default.world
<?xml version="1.0" ?>
<!--
  Default Gazebo World for Robot Simulation

  NON-REAL-TIME, NON-CERTIFIED, NON-AUTHORITATIVE
  For development and testing only.
-->
<sdf version="1.6">
  <world name="default">
    <!-- Lighting -->
    <include>
      <uri>model://sun</uri>
    </include>

    <!-- Ground Plane -->
    <include>
      <uri>model://ground_plane</uri>
    </include>

    <!-- Physics settings (non-real-time) -->
    <physics type="ode">
      <max_step_size>0.001</max_step_size>
      <real_time_factor>1.0</real_time_factor>

ReadFile

move_group.launch.py
"""
MoveIt Move Group Launch File
Launches the MoveIt planning pipeline (NON-REAL-TIME, REQUEST ONLY)

Authority: REQUEST ONLY - generates trajectories, does not control motors
The Hardware Bridge relays trajectories to the RT Controller for execution
"""
from launch import LaunchDescription
from launch.actions import DeclareLaunchArgument
from launch.substitutions import LaunchConfiguration, PathJoinSubstitution
from launch_ros.actions import Node
from launch_ros.substitutions import FindPackageShare


def generate_launch_description():
    # Declare arguments
    use_sim_time = LaunchConfiguration('use_sim_time', default='false')

    # Package paths
    robot_description_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_description')
    moveit_config_pkg = FindPackageShare('robot_moveit_config')

    # Robot description
    robot_description_path = PathJoinSubstitution([
        robot_description_pkg, 'urdf', 'robot.urdf.xacro'
    ])

    # MoveIt configs
    kinematics_yaml = PathJoinSubstitution([
        moveit_config_pkg, 'config', 'kinematics.yaml'
    ])
    ompl_yaml = PathJoinSubstitution([
        moveit_config_pkg, 'config', 'ompl_planning.yaml'
    ])
    controllers_yaml = PathJoinSubstitution([
        moveit_config_pkg, 'config', 'controllers.yaml'
    ])
    trajectory_execution_yaml = PathJoinSubstitution([
        moveit_config_pkg, 'config', 'trajectory_execution.yaml'
    ])
    joint_limits_yaml = PathJoinSubstitution([
        robot_description_pkg, 'config', 'joint_limits.yaml'
    ])

    # Robot State Publisher
    robot_state_publisher = Node(
        package='robot_state_publisher',
        executable='robot_state_publisher',
        name='robot_state_publisher',
        output='screen',
        parameters=[{
            'robot_description': robot_description_path,
            'use_sim_time': use_sim_time,
        }]
    )

    # Move Group Node
    move_group_node = Node(
        package='moveit_ros_move_group',
        executable='move_group',
        output='screen',
        parameters=[
            {'use_sim_time': use_sim_time},
            {'robot_description': robot_description_path},
            kinematics_yaml,
            ompl_yaml,
            controllers_yaml,
            trajectory_execution_yaml,
            joint_limits_yaml,
            {'moveit_manage_controllers': True},
            {'moveit_controller_manager': 'moveit_simple_controller_manager/MoveItSimpleControllerManager'},
        ]
    )

    return LaunchDescription([
        DeclareLaunchArgument(
            'use_sim_time',
            default_value='false',
            description='Use simulation time'
        ),
        robot_state_publisher,
        move_group_node,
    ])

Thinking
Here is a comprehensive analysis of the three packages:

1. robot_description Package
Location: D:\Projects\ROBOT\6-Axis-robot-ROS2-control-movet-gazebo-\src\robot_description\

Purpose
This package contains the URDF robot model definitions, joint limits configuration, and launch files for the robot state publisher. It is the authoritative source for the robot’s kinematic description.

URDF Files (3 robot definitions)
robot.urdf.xacro – ABB IRB 120 model (6-DOF, 580mm reach, 3kg payload):

Uses a world dummy link as root, with a fixed joint to base_link.
6 revolute joints (joint_1 through joint_6) with explicit position, velocity, and effort limits derived from the ABB datasheet (e.g., joint_1: +/-165 deg, 250 deg/s).
Link masses distributed across 25kg total (base=6kg, link1=5kg, link2=6kg, link3=3kg, link4=2kg, link5=1kg, link6=0.5kg).
Visual geometry uses meshes (base_link.stl) with fallback to primitive shapes (cylinders/boxes).
Includes Gazebo Harmonic plugins inline: gz::sim::systems::JointTrajectoryController (topic /gazebo/joint_trajectory) and gz::sim::systems::JointStatePublisher (topic /gazebo/joint_states).
Has gazebo material tags for colored rendering in simulation.
Defines a tool0 end-effector frame fixed 10mm from link_6.
ur3e_cobot_gazebo.urdf.xacro – Universal Robots UR3e cobot model:

Also 6-DOF with different kinematic chain (base_link -> shoulder_link -> upper_arm_link -> forearm_link -> wrist_1/2/3_link).
Joint limits are wider (e.g., joint_1: +/-6.28 rad full rotation) with higher effort limits (330 N*m for joints 1-2).
Uses UR-style silver/blue color scheme.
Includes a <ros2_control name="GazeboSystem"> block with gz_ros2_control/GazeboSimSystem hardware plugin, defining position command interfaces and position/velocity state interfaces for all 6 joints.
Has the same Gazebo Harmonic plugins as robot.urdf.xacro.
custom_6axis_test.urdf.xacro – Generic industrial 6-DOF robot:

Heavier mass distribution (base=15kg, link1=12kg, link2=10kg, etc.).
Different kinematic chain with rotated axes (joint_2 uses pi/2 rotation, joint_4 uses -pi/2).
Also includes <ros2_control> block and Gazebo plugins.
Defines tool0 frame 20mm from link_6.
Joint Limits (config/joint_limits.yaml)
Mirrors the ABB IRB 120 datasheet values with position limits, velocity limits (e.g., joint_1 at 4.363 rad/s), and acceleration limits (10-20 rad/s^2).

Launch Files
display.launch.py – Minimal launch for URDF visualization:

Spawns robot_state_publisher with the URDF from custom_6axis_test.urdf.xacro (default).
No RViz, no controllers – purely publishes TF and robot_description.
robot.launch.py – Main orchestrator with mode selection:

Accepts mode argument (sim or real, default: sim).
Always starts display.launch.py (robot_state_publisher).
SIM mode: Includes gazebo.launch.py from robot_gazebo.
REAL mode: Launches hardware_bridge (ESP32 gateway) and moveit_adapter nodes from robot_hardware_bridge package.
Always launches MoveIt move_group.launch.py (with 10s delay for sim, 5s for real).
Always launches accuracy_node from robot_analysis.
mode_sim.launch.py – Dedicated simulation launcher:

Directly includes gazebo.launch.py and move_group.launch.py.
10-second delay before MoveIt starts (waits for Gazebo).
Launches accuracy_node.
mode_real.launch.py – Dedicated hardware launcher:

Includes display.launch.py for TF.
Launches bridge_node (ESP32 connection at 192.168.1.100) and moveit_adapter.
Launches MoveIt after 5s delay.
Launches accuracy_node.
2. robot_gazebo Package
Location: D:\Projects\ROBOT\6-Axis-robot-ROS2-control-movet-gazebo-\src\robot_gazebo\

Purpose
Gazebo Harmonic simulation environment for the robot. Provides physics emulation (explicitly noted as non-RT, non-certified).

Gazebo Launch (launch/gazebo.launch.py)
The launch sequence is carefully timed:

Gazebo Simulator (ros_gz_sim):

Two variants: headless (-r -s -v4) and GUI (-r -v4), controlled by headless argument.
Loads world file (default: empty.sdf).
Robot State Publisher:

Uses xacro to process ur3e_cobot_gazebo.urdf.xacro.
SDF Generation and Spawn:

Runs xacro to generate URDF, then gz sdf -p to convert to SDF format.
Spawns robot via ros_gz_sim create node at origin (0,0,0).
ROS-Gazebo Bridge (ros_gz_bridge):

Bridges /clock, /gazebo/joint_states, /gazebo/joint_trajectory.
Critical remappings:
/gazebo/joint_states -> /joint_states (standard ROS topic)
/gazebo/joint_trajectory -> /robot_arm_controller/joint_trajectory (controller action)
Controller Spawners (via controller_manager):

joint_state_broadcaster at T+5s.
robot_arm_controller at T+8s.
Both use 60s timeout for robustness.
Controller Configuration (config/gazebo_controllers.yaml)
controller_manager runs at 1000 Hz (simulated).
joint_state_broadcaster: Standard JSB type.
robot_arm_controller: JointTrajectoryController type with:
Joints: joint_1 through joint_6.
Command interface: position.
State interfaces: position, velocity.
Publish rate: 100 Hz, action monitor rate: 20 Hz.
No partial joint goals, no open-loop control.
Stopped velocity tolerance: 0.01 rad/s.
World File (worlds/default.world)
SDF 1.6 format with ODE physics.
Step size: 0.001s, real-time factor: 1.0, update rate: 1000 Hz.
Includes sun and ground plane models.
Camera positioned at (2.0, -2.0, 1.5) looking at origin.
3. robot_moveit_config Package
Location: D:\Projects\ROBOT\6-Axis-robot-ROS2-control-movet-gazebo-\src\robot_moveit_config\

Purpose
MoveIt 2 motion planning configuration. Generates trajectories (REQUEST only – does not control motors directly).

Move Group Launch (launch/move_group.launch.py)
Loads robot.urdf.xacro from robot_description.
Spawns robot_state_publisher and move_group node.
Merges 5 YAML configurations:
kinematics.yaml
ompl_planning.yaml
controllers.yaml
trajectory_execution.yaml
joint_limits.yaml (from robot_description)
Sets moveit_manage_controllers: true and uses MoveItSimpleControllerManager.
Controllers (config/controllers.yaml)
Single controller: robot_arm_controller.
Type: FollowJointTrajectory action.
Action namespace: bridge_controller/follow_joint_trajectory.
This is significant: MoveIt sends trajectories to /bridge_controller/follow_joint_trajectory, NOT directly to the Gazebo controller.
This routes through the Hardware Bridge node, which then relays to the actual executor (Gazebo in sim mode, ESP32 in real mode).
All 6 joints listed.
SRDF (config/robot_arm.srdf)
Defines planning group robot_arm as chain from base_link to tool0.
Predefined home state with all joints at 0.
Disables collisions between adjacent links (base_link->link_1, link_1->link_2, …, link_5->link_6).
Disables self-collision for known non-interfering pairs: link_2<->link_4, link_3<->link_5, link_3<->link_6.
OMPL Planning (config/ompl_planning.yaml)
Three planners configured: RRTConnect (default), RRTstar, PRM.
Request adapters handle constraint frames, workspace bounds, and start state validation.
Response adapters include Time-Optimal Trajectory Generation (TOTG) for time parameterization.
Projection evaluator uses joints 1 and 2.
Longest valid segment fraction: 0.01 (fine-grained collision checking).
Kinematics (config/kinematics.yaml)
Uses TRAC-IK solver (trac_ik_kinematics_plugin/TRAC_IKKinematicsPlugin).
Search resolution: 0.005, timeout: 0.05s, 3 attempts.
Solve type: Speed (prioritizes fast solutions over optimality).
The .bak file shows the previous configuration used KDL (kdl_kinematics_plugin/KDLKinematicsPlugin).
Trajectory Execution (config/trajectory_execution.yaml)
Execution duration scaling: 1.2 (20% tolerance on expected duration).
Goal duration margin: 0.5s.
Start tolerance: 0.01 rad.
Duration monitoring enabled.
Repeats OMPL pipeline configuration and moveit_simple_controller_manager settings.
System Architecture Summary
                           ┌─────────────────────┐
                           │   MoveIt move_group  │
                           │  (Planning, OMPL)    │
                           └──────────┬───────────┘
                                      │
                   /bridge_controller/│follow_joint_trajectory
                                      ▼
                           ┌─────────────────────┐
                           │   Hardware Bridge    │
                           │  (Relay/Adapter)     │
                           └──────┬───────┬──────┘
                                  │       │
                    SIM mode ─────┤       ├──── REAL mode
                                  ▼       ▼
                    ┌─────────────────┐ ┌──────────────┐
                    │   Gazebo Sim    │ │  ESP32 via   │
                    │  (gz_ros2_ctrl) │ │  Network     │
                    └─────────────────┘ └──────────────┘
Key architectural observations:

The URDF used by MoveIt (robot.urdf.xacro) is different from the one used by Gazebo (ur3e_cobot_gazebo.urdf.xacro). This mismatch means the kinematic models differ between planning and simulation, which would cause execution errors.

The controllers.yaml routes MoveIt to /bridge_controller/follow_joint_trajectory rather than directly to /robot_arm_controller/follow_joint_trajectory, adding an indirection layer through the hardware bridge.

Gazebo uses gz_ros2_control with a GazeboSimSystem hardware plugin, while the real hardware uses the ESP32 bridge.

Timing is carefully orchestrated: Gazebo launches first, controllers spawner at 5s and 8s, MoveIt starts at 10s (sim) or 5s (real).

run_roboforge.ps1
# RoboForge v8.0 — Master Launch Script (Windows)
# ───────────────────────────────────────────────

Write-Host "🤖 Starting RoboForge v8.0 Unified Stack..." -ForegroundColor Cyan

# 1. Check for Docker
if (!(Get-Command docker -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue)) {
    Write-Error "Docker not found. Please install Docker Desktop to proceed."
    exit
}

# 2. Cleanup old containers
Write-Host "🧹 Cleaning up previous instances..." -ForegroundColor Gray
docker compose down --remove-orphans

# 3. Build & Launch
Write-Host "🏗 Building and starting services (this may take a minute)..." -ForegroundColor Yellow
docker compose up --build -d

# 4. Wait for Frontend
Write-Host "⏳ Waiting for UI to become alive..." -ForegroundColor Gray
$maxRetries = 30
$retryCount = 0
$url = "http://localhost:3000"

while ($retryCount -lt $maxRetries) {
    try {
        $response = Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $url -UseBasicParsing -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue
        if ($response.StatusCode -eq 200) {
            Write-Host "✅ RoboForge UI is LIVE at $url" -ForegroundColor Green
            break
        }
    } catch {
        # Continue waiting
    }
    Start-Sleep -Seconds 2
    $retryCount++
    Write-Host "  . " -NoNewline
}

if ($retryCount -eq $maxRetries) {
    Write-Host "⚠️ UI startup is taking longer than expected. Check 'docker logs roboforge_frontend'." -ForegroundColor Red
} else {
    # 5. Open Browser
    Write-Host "🌐 Opening browser..." -ForegroundColor Cyan
    Start-Process $url
}

Write-Host "🚀 RoboForge is ready for Operation!" -ForegroundColor Green

    Write-Host "✅ Build Succeeded!" -ForegroundColor Green
    $exePath = Resolve-Path "src/RoboForge.Wpf/bin/Debug/net8.0-windows/RoboForge.Wpf.exe"
    Write-Host "🚀 Executable: $exePath" -ForegroundColor Cyan
} else {
    Write-Error "❌ Build Failed. Check the errors above."

Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the entire system. Here’s the analysis:

What’s Happening — Complete Workflow Analysis
Project Overview
This is RoboForge v8.0 — a unified robotics development platform for programming, simulating, and deploying a 6-axis industrial robot arm. It supports both simulation mode (Gazebo) and real hardware mode (ESP32 motor controller).

Architecture Layers

Core Workflow
1. Program Creation (UI Layer)

User programs robot movements via block-based editor, code editor, or manual jogging in the React UI (port 3000) or WPF desktop app
Waypoints are placed in a 3D viewport (Three.js)
IK solutions are computed either locally (JS analytical/numerical) or via MoveIt /compute_ik service
2. Trajectory Generation (MoveIt)

Program is compiled into a JointTrajectory message
MoveIt plans collision-free paths using OMPL planners (RRTConnect default)
Trajectories are time-parameterized with TOTG and sent to /bridge_controller/follow_joint_trajectory
3. Bridge Relay (Hardware Bridge)

robot_hardware_bridge receives trajectories, validates schema (joint names, array lengths)
Routes to the appropriate backend:
SIM mode: Forwards to Gazebo’s /robot_arm_controller/joint_trajectory or interpolates internally (FAKE mode)
REAL mode: Sends binary TCP protocol to ESP32 at 192.168.1.100:5000
4. Execution (Backend)

Gazebo: gz_ros2_control plugin drives simulated servos at 1000Hz with physics
ESP32 Firmware: Reads binary trajectory commands, drives PCA9685 PWM servo driver via I2C, reads quadrature encoders for feedback, publishes /joint_states at 25Hz
5. Feedback Loop

Encoder/simulation state publishes to /joint_states
accuracy_node compares planned vs actual positions, logs RMSE
gazebo_error_node (live mode) compares simulation vs real encoder data
UI displays tracking errors in real-time
Launch Flow (run_roboforge.ps1)
docker compose down          # Cleanup
docker compose up --build -d # Build & start all services
Wait for http://localhost:3000
Open browser
Docker Services:

Service	Container	Purpose
ros_core	roboforge_core	Robot description, state publisher
moveit	roboforge_moveit	Motion planning (OMPL)
pseudo_hardware	roboforge_pseudo_hw	250Hz joint_states simulator
bridge	roboforge_bridge	WebSocket (9090) + REST API (8765)
frontend	roboforge_frontend	React UI on port 3000
gazebo	roboforge_gazebo	Physics simulation (optional profile)
Key Files
File	Role
robot.urdf	URDF model (6 revolute joints, gz_ros2_control plugin)
test.sdf	SDF equivalent for Gazebo direct loading
platformio.ini	ESP32 firmware build config (WiFi/Serial controller)
docker-compose.yml	Service orchestration
hardware_config.h	ESP32 pin mappings for encoders & servos
controller/hardware_map.yaml	Joint-to-hardware mapping
bridge-server/server.js	Standalone mock rosbridge (no real ROS2)
Current State
The pipeline_diagnostic_report.json shows the system cannot connect to rosbridge — Docker is likely not running or the bridge service failed. The error: [WinError 1225] The remote computer refused the network connection on port 9090.

There’s also a preprocessor bug in firmware/serial_control/src/main.cpp where #endif placement would cause compilation failure in DC motor mode.
